<span id="freeTextContainer12767481382408939902">This is Terry Brooks' true masterpiece in my eyes, and still my personal favourite in the Shannara series. I would actually place it in the top three within the fantasy genre, and it even had a scene that put a tear in my eye (everyone who has read the book knows which one).<br/><br/>It started out quite weakly. As always, Allanon's appearance to an Ohmsford was repeated, and in contrast to the same scenes in the two previous books, this one was quite boring. Also, that the main "villain" of the story was</span>
  <span id="freeText12767481382408939902" style="display:none">This is Terry Brooks' true masterpiece in my eyes, and still my personal favourite in the Shannara series. I would actually place it in the top three within the fantasy genre, and it even had a scene that put a tear in my eye (everyone who has read the book knows which one).<br /><br />It started out quite weakly. As always, Allanon's appearance to an Ohmsford was repeated, and in contrast to the same scenes in the two previous books, this one was quite boring. Also, that the main "villain" of the story was the evil book that once corrupted the rebel druid Brona, seemed at first to be rather inadequate for an epic fantasy villain like these books have to have. Deep inside, I feared that this one wouldn't get anywhere near <i>Sword</i> and <i>Elfstones</i>. But despite my worst fears, I kept reading. I'm rather pleased with that decision now.<br /><br />The main characters, the siblings Brin and Jair Ohmsford, are simply perfect. The supporting characters are absolutely brilliant as well, among them Allanon (of course), Garet Jax the invincible Weapons Master and Slanter the Gnome Tracker. The magic system is new and interesting, the villains are mysterious and fascinating, the locations are intriguing and the development of Brin's and Jair's stories is amazingly well done. All in all, the <i>Wishsong</i> is so close to completely flawless that the few downsides don't even make a difference.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4120500669013559460">I have to admit that I started reading Shannara when <b>The Sword of Shannara</b> came out in the late 70's. Don't have a clue how many times I've read it since, and the same goes for both this one and <b>The Elfstones of Shannara</b>. Because of that, I can't possibly give this book any less than 5 stars. While the first book is a bit like the Tolkein books, the second and third books move off into their own world and leave the <b>Lord of the Rings</b> far behind going its own way. Unfortunately, my review of this </span>
  <span id="freeText4120500669013559460" style="display:none">I have to admit that I started reading Shannara when <b>The Sword of Shannara</b> came out in the late 70's. Don't have a clue how many times I've read it since, and the same goes for both this one and <b>The Elfstones of Shannara</b>. Because of that, I can't possibly give this book any less than 5 stars. While the first book is a bit like the Tolkein books, the second and third books move off into their own world and leave the <b>Lord of the Rings</b> far behind going its own way. Unfortunately, my review of this book boils down to: <i>"This is one of my favorite series, and I really enjoy reading/listening to it."</i>. Is there anything else to say? &lt;&gt;&lt;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2263853161" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9643366221244984365">I want to thank <a href='https://blogger.randomhouse.de/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bloggerportal</a> and <a href='https://www.randomhouse.de/Taschenbuch/Die-Shannara-Chroniken-3-Das-Lied-der-Elfen/Terry-Brooks/Blanvalet-Taschenbuch/e515289.rhd' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blanvalet</a> for giving me the opportunity to read this novel. They were so great to give me <i>The Wishsong of Shannara</i> in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>You also are able to read this review on my blog <a href='https://blattzirkus.wordpress.com/2018/02/19/de-eng-review-the-shannara-chronicles-the-wishsong-of-shannara-by-terry-brooks/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blattzirkus</a>.<br/><br/>--<br/><br/><b>Abstract</b><br/>An age-old threat returns to the world, sending out its Mord Wraiths to destroy humanity and the elves. To repress and defeat this power, the Druid Allanon needs the support of Brin Ohmsford, the guardian of the Elfstones. Because only Brin contro</span>
  <span id="freeText9643366221244984365" style="display:none">I want to thank <a href="https://blogger.randomhouse.de/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloggerportal</a> and <a href="https://www.randomhouse.de/Taschenbuch/Die-Shannara-Chroniken-3-Das-Lied-der-Elfen/Terry-Brooks/Blanvalet-Taschenbuch/e515289.rhd" rel="nofollow noopener">Blanvalet</a> for giving me the opportunity to read this novel. To repress and defeat this power, the Druid Allanon needs the support of Brin Ohmsford, the guardian of the Elfstones. Because only Brin controls the magic song of the elves. But evil has foreseen Allanon’s move, and Brin is now waiting for a fate worse than death. I like both cover arts, but please stick with one style. Else it doesn’t look good on the bookshelf and it seems as if the books don’t belong together. Thanks 😀<br /><br /><b>The Author: Terry Brooks</b><br />Terry Brooks is an US-American Fantasy-Author who published his first book, The Shannara-Chronicles: The Sword of Shannara, in 1977. Before his breakthrough as a writer, Brooks was working as a lawyer. He gave up on this job after his sales success with his book.<br /><br /><i>After Terry Brooks’ German <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a> page (July 17th, 2018)</i><br /><br /><b>Book Trilogy</b><br />In this review I will review Book 3, The Wishsong of Shannara. I have already reviewed Book 1, The Sword of Shannara and Book 2, The Elfstones of Shannara. If anyone is going to continue reading this review – you are warned. This might get spoilery.<br /><br /><b>My Opinion</b><br />The Wishsong of Shannara was better to read for me than Book 1, The Sword of Shannara. However, I gave the book no more and no less stars than The Sword of Shannara, two stars. How these two books nevertheless differ from each other and what I liked better about The Wishsong of Shannara, I try to explain a little in the next few paragraphs.<br /><br />First of all, it did seem like a cheap rip-off of Lord of the Rings. I could draw a lot of parallels in The Sword of Shannara, which bothered me so much because The Shannara Chronicles should be a fantasy world after all and not a Lord of the Rings copy. But do not worry, that was only the case in Book 1. Book 2 and 3 felt much more like an own world and that’s a good thing.<br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br />What bothered me about The Wishsong of Shannara is the fact that there never was exciting action, at least in my eyes. Two groups go from A and B, battles are interspersed every now and then, and that’s it. Maybe it’s because of Terry Brooks’ writing style, but I never had the feeling that the characters could not accomplish their mission. There was never the moment in which I was captivated by the story. For me, the plot was just monotone.<br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br />Character depth, what is this? I know almost as much about the druid Allanon after three books as at the beginning of the trilogy. He is always described as mysterious and secret keeping, because he literally reveals nothing about himself and if, then only the most necessary bits. This is also how it is described in the book. So it does not surprise me so much that I hardly know anything about Allanon, but hey, the reader has been informed that we should not expect too much information.<br /><br />Brin and Jair Ohmsford are the children of Wil and Eretria, from The Elfstones of Shannara, who have had a weak character development, if any. If I had the feeling – oh, they have improved their personalities! – then it was reversed again (see towards the end scene). In any case, my personal highlight was that Wil and Eretria were mentioned again and that Terry Brooks continued to travel with Ohmsford characters.<br /><br />Hardly anyone was unsympathetic, only I just wasn’t able to become friends with them, as they (as already mentioned in the paragraph above) had little depth and seemed very superficial to me.<br /><br /><b>Writing Style</b><br />Why are the characters most often called or described either by their origin or their race? Okay, in the beginning of the book, some members of the group can’t stand each other, but how should I learn names if only the race or the origin is mentioned most of the time?<br /><br /> <blockquote>“Boy!” The gnome called with a mixture of concern and relief in his voice and rushed toward the valley dweller. </blockquote><br /><br /><i>* Terry Brooks, The Shannara Chronicles: The Song of the Elves, 1986, Chapter 46, p. 497 (eBook). Roughly translated from German to English.</i><br /><br />Okay, that’s just an extreme example of a few sentences, but still. The hyper-objective salutation and partially swollen language may now be a fantasy element. After a while it became very exhausting for me and I could not really bring myself getting into the story. What a pity, because I like to remember of the good times I had while reading The Elfstones of Shannara.<br /><br />If I remember rightly, I had the problem with The Sword of Shannara and The Elfstones of Shannara, that Terry Brooks likes to describe fights and pretty much everything in a long dragging time. I still had this problem and it did not improve with The Wishsong of Shannara.<br /><br /><b>Not, that I am only complaining…</b><br />It may seem that I have been pretty hard on the book. There are certainly a lot of people who can be enthusiastic about this book (several reviews prove that). In retrospect, it’s not a bad book, the writing style is clean but it’s just not mine. Although, better to read the writing style of Terry Brooks as one who is incredibly persistent in trying to write beautifully and cumbersome (American YA writers love that).<br /><br />The plot could be better, but also far worse. In addition, I must keep in mind after all that this book has been published in 1977. It would therefore be interesting to read a Terry Brooks book from the present (2018). But until I get that far, I have to take a little distance from the book series.<br /><br /><b>Conclusion</b><br />I give The Shannara-Chronicles: The Wishsong of Shannara by Terry Brooks 2 out of 5 stars. It couldn’t convince me to like it and I wasn’t able to get into the story. But I can imagine that it’s just me and that a lot of reader will like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9643366221244984365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

There was enough differences that it was an enjoyable enough read I just wish it had managed to separate itself a little more from the books that it took inspiration from, its a narrow line between inspiration and simply ripping off and I think this skimmed the line a little to closely </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tdJaQSrnoQHeLcTXv3rH8dhl7IJazfzzIpTlY8wypf7ae89neEYcw7d1POBlQFmg/h7XMaqIfGaLpx4BurLSOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TFhrje4r9vvlv6DLV9ydwVngF5HNGRsRDoPnX0M4t0kj8f6rvIpLOYznWPyN5gOQf5ssIj1cm4SnsBw9NbjAjw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks">About Terry Brooks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1280785812p3/9629.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks">Terry Brooks
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
76,970
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1197429544508379299">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word & Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his</span>
  <span id="freeText1197429544508379299" style="display:none">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word &amp; Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his graduate degree from the School of Law at Washington &amp; Lee University.<br />A writer since high school, he wrote many stories within the genres of science fiction, western, fiction, and non-fiction, until one semester early in his college years he was given The Lord of the Rings to read. That moment changed Terry's life forever, because in Tolkien's great work he found all the elements needed to fully explore his writing combined in one genre.<br />He then wrote The Sword of Shannara, the seven year grand result retaining sanity while studying at Washington &amp; Lee University and practicing law. It became the first work of fiction ever to appear on the New York Times trade paperback bestseller list, where it remained for over five months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1197429544508379299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
